This implementation does not guarantee that only one\\n20: // client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\\n21: //\\n22: // A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\\n23: // leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\\n24: // election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\\n25: // produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\\n26: // accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\\n27: // renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\\n28: // clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\\n29: //\\n30: // However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\\n31: // RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\\n32: // maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\\n33: // the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\\n34: // the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\\n35: // to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\\n36: // the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\\n37: //\\n38: // While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\\n39: // cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\\n40: // this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\\n41: // availability.\\n42: //\\n43: // Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\\n44: // taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\\n45: // should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\\n46: // until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\\n47: // when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\\n48: // to master availability.\\n49: //\\n50: // DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. \\tLock rl.Interface\\n119: \\n120: \\t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\\n121: \\t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\\n122: \\t// last observed ack.\\n123: \\t//\\n124: \\t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\\n125: \\t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\\n126: \\t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\\n127: \\t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\\n128: \\t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\\n129: \\t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\\n130: \\t// long waits in the scenario.\\n131: \\t//\\n132: \\t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\\n133: \\tLeaseDuration time.Duration\\n134: \\t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\\n135: \\t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\\n136: \\t//\\n137: \\t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\\n138: \\tRenewDeadline time.Duration\\n139: \\t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\\n140: \\t// between tries of actions.\\n141: \\t//\\n142: \\t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\\n143: \\tRetryPeriod time.Duration\\n144: \\n145: \\t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\\n146: \\t// events of the LeaderElector\\n147: \\tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\\n148: \\n149: \\t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\\n150: \\t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\\n151: \\tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\\n152: \\n153: \\t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\\n154: \\t// when the run context is cancelled. governing permissions and\\n14: limitations under the License.\\n15: */\\n16: \\n17: // Package leaderelection implements leader election of a set of endpoints.\\n18: // It uses an annotation in the endpoints object to store the record of the\\n19: // election state. This implementation does not guarantee that only one\\n20: // client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\\n21: //\\n22: // A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\\n23: // leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\\n24: // election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\\n25: // produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\\n26: // accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\\n27: // renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\\n28: // clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\\n29: //\\n30: // However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\\n31: // RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\\n32: // maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\\n33: // the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\\n34: // the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\\n35: // to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\\n36: // the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\\n37: //\\n38: // While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\\n39: // cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\\n40: // this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\\n41: // availability.\\n42: //\\n43: // Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\\n44: // taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\\n45: // should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\\n46: // until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\\n47: // when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\\n48: // to master availability.\\n49: //\\n50: // DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\\n51: // or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. Depend on this API at\\n52: // your own risk.\\n53: package leaderelection\\n54: \\n55: import (\\n56: \\t\\\"bytes\\\"\\n57: \\t\\\"context\\\"\\n58: \\t\\\"fmt\\\"\\n59: \\t\\\"sync\\\"\\n60: \\tle.metrics.leaderOff(le.config.Name)\\n113: \\treturn &le, nil\\n114: }\\n115: \\n116: type LeaderElectionConfig struct {\\n117: \\t// Lock is the resource that will be used for locking\\n118: \\tLock rl.Interface\\n119: \\n120: \\t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\\n121: \\t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\\n122: \\t// last observed ack.\\n123: \\t//\\n124: \\t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\\n125: \\t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\\n126: \\t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\\n127: \\t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\\n128: \\t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\\n129: \\t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\\n130: \\t// long waits in the scenario.\\n131: \\t//\\n132: \\t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\\n133: \\tLeaseDuration time.Duration\\n134: \\t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\\n135: \\t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\\n136: \\t//\\n137: \\t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\\n138: \\tRenewDeadline time.Duration\\n139: \\t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\\n140: \\t// between tries of actions.\\n141: \\t//\\n142: \\t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\\n143: \\tRetryPeriod time.Duration\\n144: \\n145: \\t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\\n146: \\t// events of the LeaderElector\\n147: \\tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\\n148: \\n149: \\t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\\n150: \\t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\\n151: \\tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\\n152: \\n153: \\t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\\n154: \\t// when the run context is cancelled. Returns true on success else returns\\n351: // false.\\n352: func (le *LeaderElector) tryCoordinatedRenew(ctx context.Context) bool {\\n353: \\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\\n354: \\tnow := metav1.NewTime(le.clock.Now())\\n355: \\tleaderElectionRecord := rl.LeaderElectionRecord{\\n356: \\t\\tHolderIdentity:       le.config.Lock.Identity(),\\n357: \\t\\tLeaseDurationSeconds: int(le.config.LeaseDuration / time.Second),\\n358: \\t\\tRenewTime:            now,\\n359: \\t\\tAcquireTime:          now,\\n360: \\t}\\n361: \\n362: \\t// 1. obtain the electionRecord\\n363: \\toldLeaderElectionRecord, oldLeaderElectionRawRecord, err := le.config.Lock.Get(ctx)\\n364: \\tif err != nil {\\n365: \\t\\tif !errors.IsNotFound(err) {\\n366: \\t\\t\\tlogger.Error(err, \\\"Error retrieving lease lock\\\", \\\"lock\\\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\\n367: \\t\\t\\treturn false\\n368: \\t\\t}\\n369: \\t\\tlogger.Info(\\\"Lease lock not found\\\", \\\"lock\\\", le.config.Lock.Describe(), \\\"err\\\", err)\\n370: \\t\\treturn false\\n371: \\t}\\n372: \\n373: \\t// 2. Record obtained, check the Identity & Time\\n374: \\tif !bytes.Equal(le.observedRawRecord, oldLeaderElectionRawRecord) {\\n375: \\t\\tle.setObservedRecord(oldLeaderElectionRecord)\\n376: \\n377: \\t\\tle.observedRawRecord = oldLeaderElectionRawRecord\\n378: \\t}\\n379: \\n380: \\tle.observedRecordLock.RLock()\\n381: \\tobsTime := le.observedTime\\n382: \\tle.observedRecordLock.RUnlock()\\n383: \\n384: \\thasExpired := obsTime.Add(time.Second * time.Duration(oldLeaderElectionRecord.LeaseDurationSeconds)).Before(now.Time)\\n385: \\tif hasExpired {\\n386: \\t\\tlogger.Info(\\\"Lease has expired\\\", \\\"lock\\\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\\n387: \\t\\treturn false\\n388: \\t}\\n389: \\n390: \\tif !le.IsLeader() {\\n391: \\t\\tlogger.V(6).Info(\\\"Lease is held and has not yet expired\\\", \\\"lock\\\", le.config.Lock.Describe(), \\\"holder\\\", oldLeaderElectionRecord.HolderIdentity)\\n392: \\t\\treturn false\\n393: \\t}\\n394: \\n395: \\t// 2b. If the lease has been marked as \\\"end of term\\\", don't renew it\\n396: \\tif le.IsLeader() && oldLeaderElectionRecord.PreferredHolder != \\\"\\\" {\\n397: \\t\\tlogger.V(4).Info(\\\"Lease is marked as 'end of term'\\\", \\\"lock\\\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\\n398: \\t\\t// TODO: Instead of letting lease expire, the holder may deleted it directly\\n399: \\t\\t// This will not be compatible with all controllers, so it needs to be opt-in behavior.\\n400: \\t\\t// We must ensure all code guarded by this lease has successfully completed\\n401: \\t\\t// prior to releasing or there may be two processes\\n402: \\t\\t// simultaneously acting on the critical path.\\n403: \\t\\t// Usually once this returns false, the process is terminated..\\n404: \\t\\t// xref: OnStoppedLeading\\n405: \\t\\treturn false\\n406: \\t}\\n407: \\n408: \\t// 3. We're going to try to update. The leaderElectionRecord is set to it's default\\n409: \\t// here. Let's correct it before updating.\\n410: \\tif le.IsLeader() {\\n411: \\t\\tleaderElectionRecord.AcquireTime = oldLeaderElectionRecord.AcquireTime\\n412: \\t\\tleaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions = oldLeaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions\\n413: \\t\\tleaderElectionRecord.Strategy = oldLeaderElectionRecord.Strategy\\n414: \\t\\tle.metrics.slowpathExercised(le.config.Name)\\n415: \\t} else {\\n416: \\t\\tleaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions = oldLeaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions + 1\\n417: \\t}\\n418: \\n419: \\t// update the lock itself\\n420: \\tif err = le.config.Lock.Update(ctx, leaderElectionRecord); err != nil {\\n421: \\t\\tlogger.Error(err, \\\"Failed to update lock\\\", \\\"lock\\\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\\n422: \\t\\treturn false\\n423: \\t}\\n424: \\n425: \\tle.setObservedRecord(&leaderElectionRecord)\\n426: \\treturn true\\n427: }\\n428: \\n429: // tryAcquireOrRenew tries to acquire a leader lease if it is not already acquired,\\n430: // else it tries to renew the lease if it has already been acquired. Returns true\\n431: // on success else returns false.\\n432: func (le *LeaderElector) tryAcquireOrRenew(ctx context.Context) bool {\\n433: \\tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\\n434: \\tnow := metav1.NewTime(le.clock.Now())\\n435: \\tleaderElectionRecord := rl.LeaderElectionRecord{\\n436: \\t\\tHolderIdentity:       le.config.Lock.Identity(),\\n437: \\t\\tLeaseDurationSeconds: int(le.config.LeaseDuration / time.Second),\\n438: \\t\\tRenewTime:            now,\\n439: \\t\\tAcquireTime:          now,\\n440: \\t}\\n441: \\n442: \\t// 1. fast path for the leader to update optimistically assuming that the record observed\\n443: \\t// last time is the current version.\\n444: \\tif le.IsLeader() && le.isLeaseValid(now.Time) {\\n445: \\t\\toldObservedRecord := le.getObservedRecord()\\n446: \\t\\tleaderElectionRecord.AcquireTime = oldObservedRecord.AcquireTime\\n447: \\t\\tleaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions = oldObservedRecord.LeaderTransitions\\n448: \\n449: \\t\\terr := le.config.Lock.Update(ctx, leaderElectionRecord)\\n450: \\t\\tif err == nil {\\n451: \\t\\t\\tle.setObservedRecord(&leaderElectionRecord)\\n452: \\t\\t\\treturn true\\n453: \\t\\t}\\n454: \\t\\tlogger.Error(err, \\\"Failed to update lease optimistically, falling back to slow path\\\", \\\"lock\\\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\\n455: \\t}\\n456: \\n457: \\t// 2. obtain or create the ElectionRecord\\n458: \\toldLeaderElectionRecord, oldLeaderElectionRawRecord, err := le.config.Lock.Get(ctx)\\n459: \\tif err != nil {\\n460: \\t\\tif !errors.IsNotFound(err) {\\n461: \\t\\t\\tlogger.Error(err, \\\"Error retrieving lease lock\\\", \\\"lock\\\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\\n462: \\t\\t\\treturn false\\n463: \\t\\t}\\n464: \\t\\tif err = le.config.Lock.Create(ctx, leaderElectionRecord); err != nil {\\n465: \\t\\t\\tlogger.Error(err, \\\"Error initially creating lease lock\\\", \\\"lock\\\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\\n466: \\t\\t\\treturn false\\n467: \\t\\t}\\n468: \\n469: \\t\\tle.setObservedRecord(&leaderElectionRecord)\\n470: \\n471: \\t\\treturn true\\n472: \\t}\\n473: \\n474: \\t// 3. Record obtained, check the Identity & Time\\n475: \\tif !bytes.Equal(le.observedRawRecord, oldLeaderElectionRawRecord) {\\n476: \\t\\tle.setObservedRecord(oldLeaderElectionRecord)\\n477: \\n478: \\t\\tle.observedRawRecord = oldLeaderElectionRawRecord\\n479: \\t}\\n480: \\tif len(oldLeaderElectionRecord.HolderIdentity) > 0 && le.isLeaseValid(now.Time) && !le.IsLeader() {\\n481: \\t\\tlogger.V(4).Info(\\\"Lease is held by and has not yet expired\\\", \\\"lock\\\", le.config.Lock.Describe(), \\\"holder\\\", oldLeaderElectionRecord.HolderIdentity)\\n482: \\t\\treturn false\\n483: \\t}\\n484: \\n485: \\t// 4. We're going to try to update. The leaderElectionRecord is set to it's default\\n486: \\t// here. Let's correct it before updating.\\n487: \\tif le.IsLeader() {\\n488: \\t\\tleaderElectionRecord.AcquireTime = oldLeaderElectionRecord.AcquireTime\\n489: \\t\\tleaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions = oldLeaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions\\n490: \\t\\tle.metrics.slowpathExercised(le.config.Name)\\n491: \\t} else {\\n492: \\t\\tleaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions = oldLeaderElectionRecord.LeaderTransitions + 1\\n493: \\t}\\n494: \\n495: \\t// update the lock itself\\n496: \\tif err = le.config.Lock.Update(ctx, leaderElectionRecord); err != nil {\\n497: \\t\\tlogger.Error(err, \\\"Failed to update lease\\\", \\\"lock\\\", le.config.Lock.Describe())\\n498: \\t\\treturn false\\n499: \\t}\\n500: \\n501: \\tle.setObservedRecord(&leaderElectionRecord)\\n502: \\treturn true\\n503: }\\n504: \\n505: func (le *LeaderElector) maybeReportTransition() {\\n506: \\tif le.observedRecord.HolderIdentity == le.reportedLeader {\\n507: \\t\\treturn\\n508: \\t}\\n509: \\tle.reportedLeader = le.observedRecord.HolderIdentity\\n510: \\tif le.config.Callbacks.OnNewLeader != nil {\\n511: \\t\\tgo le.config.Callbacks.OnNewLeader(le.reportedLeader)\\n512: \\t}\\n513: }\\n514: \\n515: // Check will determine if the current lease is expired by more than timeout.\\n516: func (le *LeaderElector) Check(maxTolerableExpiredLease time.Duration) error {\\n517: \\tif !le.IsLeader() {\\n518: \\t\\t// Currently not concerned with the case that we are hot standby\\n519: \\t\\treturn nil\\n520: \\t}\\n521: \\t// If we are more than timeout seconds after the lease duration that is past the timeout\\n522: \\t// on the lease renew. Time to start reporting ourselves as unhealthy. We should have\\n523: \\t// died but conditions like deadlock can prevent this. (See #70819)\\n524: \\tle.observedRecordLock.RLock()\\n525: \\tlastObservation := le.observedTime\\n526: \\tleaseDuration := le.config.LeaseDuration\\n527: \\tle.observedRecordLock.RUnlock()\\n528: \\t}\\n532: \\n533: \\treturn nil\\n534: }\\n535: \\n536: func (le *LeaderElector) isLeaseValid(now time.Time) bool {\\n537: \\t// Lock to safely read both the time and the record\\n538: time.Duration(le.observedRecord.LeaseDurationSeconds)).After(now)\\n542: }\\n543: \\n544: // setObservedRecord will set a new observedRecord and update observedTime to the current time.\\n545: // Protect critical sections with lock.\\n546: func (le *LeaderElector) setObservedRecord(observedRecord *rl.LeaderElectionRecord) {\\n547: \\tle.observedRecordLock.Lock()\\n548: \\tdefer /*\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\n3: \n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7: \n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9: \n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: // Package leaderelection implements leader election of a set of endpoints.\n18: // It uses an annotation in the endpoints object to store the record of the\n19: // election state. This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n20: // client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n21: //\n22: // A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n23: // leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n24: // election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n25: // produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n26: // accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n27: // renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n28: // clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n29: //\n30: // However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n31: // RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n32: // maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n33: // the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n34: // the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n35: // to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n36: // the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n37: //\n38: // While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n39: // cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n40: // this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n41: // availability.\n42: //\n43: // Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n44: // taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n45: // should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n46: // until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n47: // when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n48: // to master availability.\n49: //\n50: // DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\n51: // or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. Depend on this API at\n52: // your own risk.\n53: package leaderelection\n54: \n55: import (\n56: \t\"bytes\"\n57: \t\"context\"\n58: \t\"fmt\"\n59: \t\"sync\"\n60: \t\"time\"\n61: \n62: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors\"\n63: \tmetav1 \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1\"\n64: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\"\n65: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\"\n66: \trl \"k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock\"\n67: \t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n68: \t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n69: )\n70: \n71: const (\n72: \tJitterFactor = 1.2\n73: )\n74: \n75: // NewLeaderElector creates a LeaderElector from a LeaderElectionConfig\n76: func NewLeaderElector(lec LeaderElectionConfig) (*LeaderElector, error) {\n77: \tif lec.LeaseDuration <= lec.RenewDeadline {\n78: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than renewDeadline\")\n79: \t}\n80: \tif lec.RenewDeadline <= time.Duration(JitterFactor*float64(lec.RetryPeriod)) {\n81: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than retryPeriod*JitterFactor\")\n82: \t}\n83: \tif lec.LeaseDuration < 1 {\n84: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than zero\")\n85: \t}\n86: \tif lec.RenewDeadline < 1 {\n87: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than zero\")\n88: \t}\n89: \tif lec.RetryPeriod < 1 {\n90: \t\treturn nil, \t}\n95: \tif lec.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading == nil {\n96: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"OnStoppedLeading callback must not be nil\")\n97: \t}\n98: \n99: \tif lec.Lock == nil {\n100: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"Lock must not be nil.\")\n101: \t}\n102: \tid := lec.Lock.Identity()\n103: \tif id == \"\" {\n104: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"Lock identity is empty\")\n105: \t}\n106: \n107: \tle := LeaderElector{\n108: \t\tconfig:  lec,\n109: \t\tclock:   clock.RealClock{},\n110: \t\tmetrics: globalMetricsFactory.newLeaderMetrics(),\n111: \t}\n112: \tle.metrics.leaderOff(le.config.Name)\n113: \treturn &le, nil\n114: }\n115: \n116: type LeaderElectionConfig struct {\n117: \t// Lock is the resource that will be used for locking\n118: \tLock rl.Interface\n119: \n120: \t// LeaseDuration is the duration that non-leader candidates will\n121: \t// wait to force acquire leadership. This is measured against time of\n122: \t// last observed ack.\n123: \t//\n124: \t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\n125: \t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\n126: \t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\n127: \t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\n128: \t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\n129: \t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\n130: \t// long waits in the scenario.\n131: \t//\n132: \t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\n133: \tLeaseDuration time.Duration\n134: \t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\n135: \t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\n136: \t//\n137: \t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\n138: \tRenewDeadline time.Duration\n139: \t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\n140: \t// between tries of actions.\n141: \t//\n142: \t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\n143: \tRetryPeriod time.Duration\n144: \n145: \t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\n146: \t// events of the LeaderElector\n147: \tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\n148: \n149: \t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\n150: \t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\n151: \tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\n152: \n153: \t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\n154: \t// when the run context is cancelled. If you set this to true, you must\n155: \t// ensure all code guarded by this lease has successfully completed\n156: \t// prior to cancelling the context, or you may have two processes\n157: \t// simultaneously acting on the critical path.\n158: \tReleaseOnCancel bool\n159: \n160: \t// Name is the name of the resource lock for debugging\n161: \tName string\n162: \n163: \t// Coordinated will use the Coordinated Leader Election feature\n164: \t// WARNING: Coordinated leader election is ALPHA.\n165: \tCoordinated bool\n166: }\n167: \n168: // LeaderCallbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain\n169: // lifecycle events of the LeaderElector. These are invoked asynchronously.\n170: //\n171: // possible future callbacks:\n172: //   - OnChallenge()\n173: type LeaderCallbacks struct {\n174: \t// OnStartedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client starts leading\n175: \tOnStartedLeading func(context.Context)\n176: \t// OnStoppedLeading is called when a LeaderElector client stops leading.\n177: \t// This callback is always called when the LeaderElector exits, even if it did not start leading.\n178: \t// Users should not assume that OnStoppedLeading is only called after OnStartedLeading.\n179: \t// see: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/pull/127675#discussion_r1780059887\n180: \tOnStoppedLeading func()\n181: \t// OnNewLeader is called when the client observes a leader that is\n182: \t// not the previously observed leader. This includes the first observed\n183: \t// leader when the client starts.\n184: \tOnNewLeader func(identity string)\n185: }\n186: \n187: // LeaderElector is a leader election client.\n188: type LeaderElector struct {\n189: \tconfig LeaderElectionConfig\n190: \t// internal bookkeeping\n191: \tobservedRecord    rl.LeaderElectionRecord\n192: \tobservedRawRecord []byte\n193: \tobservedTime      time.Time\n194: \t// used to implement OnNewLeader(), may lag slightly from the\n195: \t// value observedRecord.HolderIdentity if the transition has\n196: \t// not yet been reported.\n197: \treportedLeader string\n198: \n199: \t// clock is wrapper around time to allow for less flaky testing\n200: \tclock clock.Clock\n201: \n202: \t// used to lock the observedRecord and the observedTime\n203: \tobservedRecordLock sync.RWMutex\n204: \n205: \tmetrics leaderMetricsAdapter\n206: }\n207: \n208: // Run starts the leader election loop. Run will not return\n209: // before leader election loop is stopped by ctx or it has\n210: // stopped holding the leader lease\n211: func (le *LeaderElector) Run(ctx context.Context) {\n212: \tdefer runtime.HandleCrashWithContext(ctx)\n213: \tdefer le.config.Callbacks.OnStoppedLeading()\n214: \n215: \tif !le.acquire(ctx) {\n216: \t\treturn // ctx signalled done\n217: \t}\n218: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n219: \tdefer cancel()\n220: \tgo le.config.Callbacks.OnStartedLeading(ctx)\n221: \tle.renew(ctx)\n222: }\n223: \n224: // RunOrDie starts a client with the provided config or panics if the config\n225: // fails to validate. RunOrDie blocks until leader election loop is\n226: // stopped by ctx or it has stopped holding the leader lease\n227: func RunOrDie(ctx context.Context, lec LeaderElectionConfig) {\n228: \tle, err := NewLeaderElector(lec)\n229: \tif err != nil {\n230: \t\tpanic(err)\n231: \t}\n232: \tif lec.WatchDog != nil {\n233: \t\tlec.WatchDog.SetLeaderElection(le)\n234: \t}\n235: \tle.Run(ctx)\n236: }\n237: \n238: // GetLeader returns the identity of the last observed leader or returns the empty string if\n239: // no leader has yet been observed.\n240: // This function is for informational purposes. (e.g. monitoring, logs, etc.)\n241: func (le *LeaderElector) GetLeader() string {\n242: \treturn le.getObservedRecord().HolderIdentity\n243: }\n244: \n245: // IsLeader returns true if the last observed leader was this client else returns false.\n246: func (le *LeaderElector) IsLeader() bool {\n247: \treturn le.getObservedRecord().HolderIdentity == le.config.Lock.Identity()\n248: }\n249: \n250: // acquire loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew and returns true immediately when tryAcquireOrRenew succeeds.\n251: // Returns false if ctx signals done.\n252: func (le *LeaderElector) acquire(ctx context.Context) bool {\n253: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n254: \tdefer cancel()\n255: \tsucceeded := false\n256: \tdesc := le.config.Lock.Describe()\n257: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n258: \tlogger.Info(\"Attempting to acquire leader lease...\", \"lock\", desc)\n259: \twait.JitterUntilWithContext(ctx, func(ctx context.Context) {\n260: \t\tif !le.config.Coordinated {\n261: \t\t\tsucceeded = le.tryAcquireOrRenew(ctx)\n262: \t\t} else {\n263: \t\t\tsucceeded = le.tryCoordinatedRenew(ctx)\n264: \t\t}\n265: \t\tle.maybeReportTransition()\n266: \t\tif !succeeded {\n267: \t\t\tlogger.V(4).Info(\"Failed to acquire lease\", \"lock\", desc)\n268: \t\t\treturn\n269: \t\t}\n270: \t\tle.config.Lock.RecordEvent(\"became leader\")\n271: \t\tle.metrics.leaderOn(le.config.Name)\n272: \t\tlogger.Info(\"Successfully acquired lease\", \"lock\", desc)\n273: \t\tcancel()\n274: \t}, le.config.RetryPeriod, JitterFactor, true)\n275: \treturn succeeded\n276: }\n277: \n278: // renew loops calling tryAcquireOrRenew and returns immediately when tryAcquireOrRenew fails or ctx signals done.\n279: func (le *LeaderElector) renew(ctx context.Context) {\n280: \tdefer le.config.Lock.RecordEvent(\"stopped leading\")\n281: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n282: \tdefer cancel()\n283: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n284: \twait.UntilWithContext(ctx, func(ctx context.Context) {\n285: \t\terr := wait.PollUntilContextTimeout(ctx, le.config.RetryPeriod, le.config.RenewDeadline, true, func(ctx context.Context) (done bool, err error) {\n286: \t\t\t// PollUntilContextTimeout invokes condition even when the context is canceled when immediate=true.\n287: \t\t\t// Short-circuit this to prevent unnecessary processing and error log messages.\n288: \t\t\tif err := ctx.Err(); err != nil {\n289: \t\t\t\treturn false, err\n290: \t\t\t}\n291: \t\t\tif !le.config.Coordinated {\n292: \t\t\t\treturn le.tryAcquireOrRenew(ctx), nil\n293: \t\t\t} else {\n294: \t\t\t\treturn le.tryCoordinatedRenew(ctx), nil\n295: \t\t\t}\n296: \t\t})\n297: \t\tle.maybeReportTransition()\n298: \t\tdesc := le.config.Lock.Describe()\n299: \t\tif err == nil {\n300: \t\t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Successfully renewed lease\", \"lock\", desc)\n301: \t\t\treturn\n302: \t\t}\n303: \t\tle.metrics.leaderOff(le.config.Name)\n304: \t\tlogger.Info(\"Failed to renew lease\", \"lock\", desc, \"err\", err)\n305: \t\tcancel()\n306: \t}, le.config.RetryPeriod)\n307: \n308: \t// if we hold the lease, give it up\n309: \tif le.config.ReleaseOnCancel {\n310: \t\tle.release(logger)\n311: \t}\n312: }\n313: \n314: // release attempts to release the leader lease if we have acquired it.\n315: func (le *LeaderElector) release(logger klog.Logger) bool {\n316: Leader Election\\n\\nKubernetes implements leader election through a **lease-based mechanism** in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`. The core component is the `LeaderElector` struct, which manages a leadership claim on a Kubernetes Lease resource.\\n\\n### Kubernetes Election Flow\\n\\nThe election process follows this sequence:\\n\\n1. **Initialization**: `NewLeaderElector()` creates a LeaderElector with a `LeaderElectionConfig` containing:\\n   - `Lock`: A `LeaseLock` (defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/leaselock.go`) that represents a Kubernetes Lease API object\\n   - `LeaseDuration`: How long the lease is valid (default 15 seconds)\\n   - `RenewDeadline`: Time to renew before giving up (default 10 seconds)\\n   - `RetryPeriod`: Interval between retries (default 2 seconds)\\n\\n2. **Leadership Acquisition**: `LeaderElector.Run()` calls `acquire()`, which repeatedly calls `tryAcquireOrRenew(ctx)` until successful. This method:\\n   - Attempts to create a new LeaderElectionRecord in the Lease if it doesn't exist\\n   - Updates the Lease with HolderIdentity, AcquireTime, and RenewTime fields\\n   - Uses fast-path optimization: if already leading, optimistically updates the record\\n   - Falls back to slow-path (full read-modify-write) on conflict\\n\\n3. **Leadership Renewal**: Once acquired, `Run()` calls `renew()`, which continuously attempts to renew the lease within `RenewDeadline` using `PollUntilContextTimeout()`. The renewal checks:\\n   - `isLeaseValid()` verifies the lease hasn't expired by checking: `observedTime + LeaseDurationSeconds > now`\\n   - If renewal fails within RenewDeadline, the process stops leading\\n\\n### Kubernetes Failover and Re-election\\n\\nFailover is **time-based** and deterministic:\\n\\n1. **Leader Detection**: When a leader dies, no renewal happens. Other candidates wait for `LeaseDuration` to expire (time since last successful renewal).\\n2. **Re-election Trigger**: Once `LeaseDuration` expires, any candidate can call `tryAcquireOrRenew()` which checks: if `len(HolderIdentity) > 0 && isLeaseValid(now) && !IsLeader()` returns false (lease expired), it attempts to acquire.\\n3. **Transition Tracking**: `maybeReportTransition()` triggers the `OnNewLeader()` callback when leadership changes detected through `LeaderElectionRecord.HolderIdentity`.\\n\\nThe implementation explicitly documents that it does NOT provide strict fencing (only one holder), relying instead on timestamps and local clocks. It's tolerant to clock skew but not to high clock skew rates.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd implements leader election through the **Raft consensus algorithm** at the server level, with an optional client-side election API wrapper.\\n\\n### etcd Server-Level Raft Election\\n\\nThe core Raft implementation is in `server/etcdserver/raft.go` in the `raftNode` struct:\\n\\n1. **Node Initialization**: `newRaftNode(cfg raftNodeConfig)` creates a raftNode that wraps a `raft.Node` with:\\n   - Periodic `tick()` calls (based on heartbeat interval, typically ~100ms)\\n   - A transport layer for sending/receiving Raft messages\\n   - Storage layer for persisting Raft state\\n\\n2. **Election Loop**: `raftNode.start()` launches a goroutine that:\\n   - Calls `tick()` on each heartbeat ticker interval\\n   - Processes `Ready()` states from the Raft node\\n   - Detects leadership changes via `rd.SoftState.Lead`\\n   - Calls `updateLeadership(newLeader)` when leadership transitions occur\\n   - The Raft state machine internally handles campaign timeout logic\\n\\n3. **Leadership State**: Leadership is determined by the Raft node's internal state:\\n   - `rd.RaftState == raft.StateLeader` indicates the node is now leader\\n   - `rd.SoftState.Lead` contains the leader's node ID\\n   - Metrics track: `isLeader.Set(1)` for leader, `leaderChanges.Inc()` on transitions\\n\\n### etcd Client-Side Election API\\n\\nFor application-level leader election, etcd provides `client/v3/concurrency/election.go`:\\n\\n1. **Campaign**: `Election.Campaign(ctx, val)` implements client-side election:\\n   - Uses a transaction: `If(v3.Compare(v3.CreateRevision(k), \\\"=\\\", 0))`\\n   - Puts a key `\\\"%s%x\\\".format(keyPrefix, lease_id)` with the election value\\n   - Waits for all keys with lower CreateRevision to be deleted via `waitDeletes()`\\n   - Only becomes leader when all previous candidates resign\\n\\n2. **Proclaim**: `Election.Proclaim(ctx, val)` allows leader to announce new values with transactional safety\\n\\n3. **Resign**: `Election.Resign(ctx)` releases leadership, allowing next candidate to become leader\\n\\n### etcd Failover and Re-election\\n\\nFailover is **automatic and consensus-based**:\\n\\n1. **Failure Detection**: When a leader fails:\\n   - Followers stop receiving heartbeats within election timeout (~150-300ms in Raft)\\n   - The Raft state machine automatically initiates `Campaign()` internally\\n   - Raft protocol ensures safe state transitions through majority quorum\\n\\n2. **Leader Election**: The Raft consensus algorithm guarantees:\\n   - A term increments on each election\\n   - A node becomes candidate, increments term, and sends RequestVote RPCs\\n   - First candidate to get majority votes becomes leader\\n   - All entries from previous leader are committed before new entries\\n\\n3. **Leadership Transition Detection**: `server/etcdserver/raft.go` lines 186-204:\\n   - `newLeader := rd.SoftState.Lead != raft.None && rh.getLead() != rd.SoftState.Lead`\\n   - On transition: `leaderChanges.Inc()` and `hasLeader.Set(1/0)`\\n   - Resets contention detector with `r.td.Reset()`\\n\\n4. **Member Changes**: Configuration changes are replayed as `raftpb.EntryConfChange` entries before followers can participate, ensuring consistency during membership updates.\\n\\n---\\n\\n## Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |\\n|--------|-----------|------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Lease-based on API objects | Raft consensus algorithm |\\n| **Failure Detection** | Time-based (LeaseDuration) | Election timeout (async heartbeat) |\\n| **Failover Speed** | Deterministic, ~LeaseDuration (15s default) | Sub-second (depends on election timeout) |\\n| **Fencing** | Not guaranteed (time-based only) | Strong consistency via quorum |\\n| **Storage** | Kubernetes Lease API | Raft log + persistent storage |\\n| **Applicability** | Controller managers, schedulers | Cluster-wide consensus, core state |\\n| **Client Integration** | Uses Lock interface with retries | Raft consensus integrated in server |\\n\""},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":4866,"cache_read_input_tokens":81398,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":4866},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"fca36210-9535-4083-87fc-014f89551b8f","uuid":"c0f5ae08-045b-448b-961a-4d1e158e5759"}
